  "article_text": [
    "among jet observables , the three - jet production rate in electron  positron annihilation plays an outstanding role .",
    "the initial experimental observation of three - jet events at petra  @xcite , in agreement with the theoretical prediction  @xcite , provided first evidence for the gluon , and thus strong support for the theory of quantum chromodynamics ( qcd ) .",
    "subsequently the three - jet rate and related event shape observables were used for the precise determination of the qcd coupling constant @xmath6 ( see  @xcite for a review ) . especially at lep",
    ", three - jet observables were measured to a very high precision and the error on the extraction of @xmath6 from these data is dominated by the uncertainty inherent in the theoretical next - to - leading order ( nlo ) calculation  @xcite of the jet observables .",
    "the planned tesla  @xcite linear @xmath7 collider will allow precision qcd studies at even higher energies than at lep .",
    "given the projected luminosity of tesla , one again expects the experimental errors to be well below the uncertainty of the nlo calculation .    related to @xmath8  jets by crossing symmetry are @xmath9-jet production in deep inelastic @xmath10 scattering and vector - boson - plus - jet production at hadron colliders .",
    "the experimental data from hera on @xmath11  jets and related event shape observables have already reached a level of precision demanding predictions beyond the present nlo accuracy ; a further improvement on these data is expected soon from the hera high luminosity programme . similarly , vector - boson production at large transverse momentum is a classic test of qcd in hadron ",
    "hadron collisions and demands the theoretical prediction to be as precise as possible . in this case",
    ", it is also an important background in searches for new physics at the tevatron and the lhc .    besides its phenomenological importance",
    ", the three - jet rate has also served as a theoretical testing ground for the development of new techniques for higher order calculations in qcd : both the subtraction  @xcite and the phase - space slicing  @xcite methods for the extraction of infrared singularities from nlo real radiation processes were developed in the context of the first three - jet calculations .",
    "the systematic formulation of phase - space slicing  @xcite as well as the dipole subtraction  @xcite method were also first demonstrated for three - jet observables , before being applied to other processes .",
    "it is very likely that similar techniques at higher orders will first be developed in the context of jet production in @xmath7 annihilation , which in contrast to hadron ",
    "hadron collisions or electron  proton scattering does not pose the additional difficulty of the regularization of initial state singularities .",
    "the calculation of next - to - next - to - leading order ( nnlo ) , i.e.   @xmath12 , corrections to the three - jet rate in @xmath7 annihilation has been considered as a highly important project for a long time  @xcite . in terms of matrix elements",
    ", it requires the computation of three contributions : the tree level @xmath13  partons amplitudes  @xcite , the one - loop corrections to the @xmath14  partons amplitudes  @xcite , and the two - loop ( as well as the one - loop times one - loop ) corrections to the @xmath15  partons matrix elements .",
    "while the former two contributions have been known for some time already , the two - loop amplitudes have presented an obstacle that prevented further progress on this calculation up to now .",
    "this calculation has now become tractable owing to various technical developments over the last two years . in particular , the systematic application of integration - by - parts  @xcite and lorentz invariance  @xcite identities allowed the large number of feynman integrals appearing in two - loop four - point matrix elements to be reduced to a small number of so - called master integrals .",
    "the use of these techniques already allowed the calculation of two - loop qed and qcd corrections to many @xmath16 scattering processes with massless on - shell external particles  @xcite , which require master integrals corresponding to massless four - point functions with all legs on - shell  @xcite .",
    "the master integrals relevant in the context of the present work are massless four - point functions with three legs on - shell and one leg off - shell .",
    "the complete set of these integrals was computed in  @xcite , earlier partial results had been presented in  @xcite .",
    "the master integrals in  @xcite are expressed in terms of two - dimensional harmonic polylogarithms ( 2dhpls ) .",
    "the 2dhpls are an extension of the harmonic polylogarithms ( hpls ) of  @xcite .",
    "all hpls and 2dhpls that appear in the divergent parts of the planar master integrals have weight @xmath17 and can be related to the more commonly known nielsen generalized polylogarithms  @xcite of suitable arguments .",
    "the functions of weight 4 appearing in the finite parts of the master integrals can all be represented , by the very definition , as one - dimensional integrals over 2dhpls of weight 3 , hence of nielsen s generalized polylogarithms of suitable arguments according to the above remark . a table with all relations is included in the appendix of  @xcite .",
    "numerical routines providing an evaluation of the hpls  @xcite and 2dhpls  @xcite are available .    in this paper , we present the @xmath0 corrections to the @xmath1 matrix element . at this order , two combinations of amplitudes",
    "contribute : the interference of two - loop and tree amplitudes and the self - interference of the one - loop amplitude .",
    "we work in conventional dimensional regularization  @xcite , with @xmath18 space - time dimensions , where all external particles are @xmath19-dimensional .",
    "ultraviolet renormalization is performed in the @xmath2 scheme .",
    "the infrared pole structure of the two - loop corrections to the @xmath1 matrix element was predicted by catani  @xcite , using an infrared factorization formula .",
    "we confirm catani s prediction with our explicit calculation , and we use the formalism introduced in  @xcite to present the infrared poles and the finite parts of the @xmath1 matrix elements in a compact form .    the paper is structured as follows . in section  [ sec :",
    "note ] , we define the notation and kinematics used in the paper . section  [ sec : method ] explains the method we used to reduce the two - loop diagrams to master integrals .",
    "the result for the two - loop qcd contribution to the @xmath1 matrix element , decomposed into infrared - divergent and infrared - finite parts according to the prescription derived in  @xcite , is given in section  [ sec : me ] .",
    "finally , section  [ sec : conc ] contains the conclusions and an outlook on future steps needed for the completion of a full nnlo calculation of three - jet production in @xmath7 annihilation .",
    "we consider the decay of a virtual photon into a quark  antiquark  gluon system : @xmath20 the kinematics of this process is fully described by the invariants @xmath21",
    "which fulfil @xmath22 it is convenient to define the dimensionless invariants @xmath23 with @xmath24 .    our calculation is performed in conventional dimensional regularization @xcite with @xmath18 , and all external particle states are taken to be @xmath19-dimensional .",
    "renormalization of ultraviolet divergences is performed in the @xmath2 scheme .",
    "the renormalized amplitude can be written as @xmath25 \\ ; , \\label{eq : renorme}\\ ] ] where @xmath26 denotes the electromagnetic coupling constant , @xmath27 the quark charge , @xmath6 the qcd coupling constant at the renormalization scale @xmath28 , and the @xmath29 are the @xmath30-loop contributions to the renormalized amplitude .",
    "they are vectors in colour space .",
    "the squared amplitude , summed over spins , colours and quark flavours , is denoted by @xmath31 the perturbative expansion of @xmath32 at renormalization scale @xmath33 reads : @xmath34 \\;,\\end{aligned}\\ ] ] where @xmath35\\;,\\\\ \\label{eq : t4 } { \\cal t}^{(4 ) } ( x , y , z ) & = &   \\langle{\\cal m}^{(0)}|{\\cal m}^{(1)}\\rangle + \\langle{\\cal m}^{(1)}|{\\cal m}^{(0)}\\rangle \\ ; , \\\\ \\label{eq : t6 } { \\cal t}^{(6 ) } ( x , y , z ) & = &   \\langle{\\cal m}^{(1)}|{\\cal m}^{(1)}\\rangle + \\langle{\\cal m}^{(0)}|{\\cal m}^{(2)}\\rangle + \\langle{\\cal m}^{(2)}|{\\cal m}^{(0)}\\rangle \\;,\\end{aligned}\\ ] ] where @xmath36 , with @xmath37 the number of colours .",
    "@xmath38 was first derived in  @xcite ; we quote an explicit expression for it in section  [ sec : irf ] . in the following , we present the contribution to @xmath39 from the interference of two - loop and tree diagrams @xmath40 ) } ( x , y , z ) =   \\langle{\\cal m}^{(0)}|{\\cal m}^{(2)}\\rangle + \\langle{\\cal m}^{(2)}|{\\cal m}^{(0)}\\rangle \\;,\\ ] ] as well as",
    "the one - loop self - interference @xmath41 ) } ( x , y , z ) =   \\langle{\\cal m}^{(1)}|{\\cal m}^{(1)}\\rangle \\;.\\ ] ] at the same order in @xmath6 , one finds also a contribution to three - jet final states from the self - interference of the @xmath42 amplitude .",
    "the matrix element for this process does not contain infrared or ultraviolet divergences ; it was computed long ago and can be found in  @xcite .    for the remainder of this paper we will set the renormalization scale @xmath43 .",
    "the full scale dependence of the perturbative expansion is given by @xmath44 \\nonumber \\\\ & & + \\left(\\frac{\\alpha_s(\\mu^2)}{2\\pi}\\right)^2 \\bigg [ { \\cal t}^{(6 ) } ( x , y , z )   + \\biggl(2b_0{\\cal t}^{(4 ) } ( x , y , z)+b_1{\\cal t}^{(2)}(x , y , z ) \\biggr )   \\ln\\left({\\mu^2\\over q^2}\\right )    \\nonumber\\\\ & & \\hspace{3 cm } + b_0 ^ 2 { \\cal t}^{(2 ) } ( x , y , z ) \\ln^2\\left({\\mu^2\\over q^2}\\right)\\bigg ]   + { \\cal o}(\\alpha_s^3 ) \\bigg\\}.\\end{aligned}\\ ] ]",
    "the feynman diagrams contributing to the @xmath30-loop amplitude @xmath29 ( @xmath45 ) were all generated using qgraf  @xcite .",
    "there are two diagrams at tree - level , 13 diagrams at one loop and 229 diagrams at two loops .",
    "we then project @xmath46 by @xmath47 and @xmath48 by @xmath49 , and perform the summation over colours and spins using the computer algebra programs maple  @xcite , form2  @xcite and form3  @xcite .",
    "when summing over the polarizations of the external gluon and off - shell photon , we use the feynman gauge : @xmath50 this is valid because the gluon always couples to a conserved fermionic current , which selects only the physical degrees of polarization .",
    "the use of an axial polarization sum to project out the transverse polarizations ( as applied in  @xcite ) is therefore not needed .",
    "the one - loop self - interference contribution @xmath51)}$ ] is computed by reducing all tensorial loop integrals according to the standard passarino ",
    "veltman procedure  @xcite to scalar one - loop two - point , three - point and four - point integrals .",
    "it has been known for a long time that those three - point integrals can be further reduced to linear combinations of two - point integrals using integration - by - parts identities .",
    "after this reduction , @xmath51)}$ ] is expressed as a bilinear combination of only two integrals : the one - loop box and the one - loop bubble , which are listed in appendix  [ app : master_int ] .",
    "the computation of @xmath52)}$ ] is by far less straightforward .",
    "it is explained in detail in the following two subsections .",
    "the integrals appearing in the individual two - loop diagrams contain up to seven propagators in the denominator , and up to four irreducible scalar products in the numerator ( i.e.  scalar products which can not be expressed as linear combinations of the occurring propagators ) .",
    "each integral is classified by the number of different denominators @xmath53 , the total number of denominators @xmath54 and the number of irreducible scalar products @xmath55 .",
    "the set of @xmath53 different denominators defines the topology of the diagram .    using the reduction procedure described in section  [ sec : red ] below , all of the two - loop feynman diagrams can be reduced to a basis set of _ master",
    "_ integrals . owing to the presence of the extra scale",
    ", there are considerably more master topologies than in the on - shell case .",
    "altogether there are 14 planar topologies and 5 non - planar topologies requiring a total of 24 master integrals , as five topologies possess two master integrals ( see below ) . for each topology , we take one of the master integrals ( or the master integral , when it is unique ) to be equal to the full scalar amplitude with the first power on all propagators .",

}   \\hfill}\\;.\\end{aligned}\\ ] ]      the reduction of the two - loop diagrams to master integrals using integration - by - parts ( ibp )  @xcite and lorentz invariance ( li )  @xcite identities was performed with two independent programs , which allowed a comparison diagram by diagram .",
    "one program was based on the reduction algorithm already described in  @xcite . in this program ,",
    "reduction equations are derived by applying the differentiation operators of the ibp and li identities to the following integrands : @xmath69 ; @xmath70 ( note that it is not necessary to include @xmath71 integrands with @xmath72 ) .",
    "as a result , one obtains a linear system of equations , which contains , besides integrals of the class @xmath73 and simpler integrals , also more complicated integrals of the classes @xmath74 and @xmath75 .",
    "the number of equations does , however , exceed the number of integrals , thus yielding an apparently overconstrained system of equations . by solving this system of equations using the computer algebra programs maple  @xcite and form2  @xcite",
    ", one expresses integrals of a given class @xmath73 as linear combinations of simpler integrals .",
    "the irreducible integrals , which are left over after this procedure , are the master integrals . compared to the algorithm used in  @xcite",
    ", one major modification was made . for integrals corresponding to those topologies which do not possess an independent master integral ( i.e.",
    "can be fully reduced to integrals with one less propagator by the ibp and li identities ) , it is straightforward to obtain a symbolic solution of the ibp and li identities .",
    "this solution takes the form of a single equation decreasing the power on one or more of the propagators ( see  @xcite for an example ) .",
    "these symbolic reduction equations for all non - master topologies were derived automatically using a form2  @xcite program .",
    "the use of these symbolic identities did lead to a considerable speed - up of the reduction of the amplitudes of such diagrams to master integrals .",
    "the second approach derived the reduction equations using the ibp and li identities for three auxiliary diagrams  one planar and two non - planar .",
    "these auxiliary diagrams are obtained by mapping the nine possible dot - products involving the three independent external momenta ( @xmath76 and @xmath77 ) and the two loop momenta as propagators .",
    "scalar products in the numerator are replaced by propagators raised to negative powers . for illustration ,",
    "the planar auxiliary diagram is shown in fig .  1",
    ", with each propagator @xmath30 raised to the arbitrary power @xmath78 .",
    "an advantage of this method is that the 10 ibp and 3 li identities are written in terms of arbitrary @xmath78 and are valid for all subtopologies of the auxiliary diagram ( @xmath79 ) and all tensor integrals ( @xmath80 )",
    ". typically we encounter subtopologies with up to 7 propagators ( @xmath81 ) and tensor integrals up to fourth rank ( @xmath71 ) . for a given value of @xmath53 , and assignment of propagators ,",
    "we generate equations using tensor integrals with @xmath82 as seeds for the generic ibp and li equations .",
    "these seed integrals are those that appear in the actual calculation of feynman diagrams .",
    "for example , for @xmath81 , there are 15 seed integrals yielding 195 equations .",
    "the equations are stored and solved one by one according to a ranking similar to that proposed by laporta  @xcite using maple  @xcite and form3  @xcite . at each stage",
    ", more complicated integrals are decomposed in terms of simpler integrals of the same topology and pinched integrals .",
    "as in the first method , the remaining irreducible integrals are master integrals .",
    "of course , the system of equations contains many more complicated integrals ( with , for example , @xmath83 or @xmath84 ) , which can not be reduced to master integrals with this approach .",
    "however , they are not needed for the evaluation of the feynman diagrams and can be eliminated from the system of equations .",
    "= 4.0 cm = 4.0 cm = 4.0 cm    in both methods , one observes that on the face of it , the planar and non - planar graphs appear to be of equal difficulty  requiring the same depth of tensor reduction with the same numbers of seed integrals and the same number of ibp and li equations .",
    "however the complexity of the non - planar graphs is first revealed in the number of terms in each equation and then in the work done to eliminate the unwanted integrals from the system of equations .",
    "both methods have their advantages .",
    "the major advantage of the first method is that the reduction equations for each topology containing master integrals have to be evaluated only once , while the second method requires their repeated evaluation each time a topology appears as subtopology of the auxiliary diagram . as a consequence ,",
    "the first method needed less computer time for the derivation of all required reduction equations .",
    "an advantage of the second method is that it needs less human intervention , since mapping of subtopologies to master topologies is not necessary , and the generalization to more complicated graphs with additional energy scales requires only the modification of the 13 ibp and li equations .",
    "the solution of the system and identification of master integrals is only limited by computer resources .",
    "the two - loop master integrals relevant to the @xmath85 matrix element are two - loop four - point functions with one leg off - shell .",
    "these functions were all computed in  @xcite in the framework of dimensional regularization with @xmath18 space - time dimensions .",
    "the results of  @xcite take the form of a laurent series in @xmath86 , starting at @xmath87 , with coefficients containing one- and two - dimensional harmonic polylogarithms  @xcite , which are a generalization of nielsen s polylogarithms  @xcite .",
    "all master integrals in  @xcite were given for one particular configuration of the external momenta .",
    "they were expressed in a form where the argument of the 2dhpls was always @xmath88 , while @xmath89 appeared in the index vector of the 2dhpls ; @xmath88 and @xmath89 appeared also as argument of the hpls .",
    "each master integral can occur in six kinematic configurations ( corresponding to the permutations of @xmath90 ) . to avoid hidden zeros ( arising from cancellations occurring in the combinations of hpls and 2dhpls with different arguments and different variables in the index vector ) , we express the master integrals for all kinematic configurations in a unique form , which is the same as in  @xcite : the argument of the 2dhpls is always @xmath88 , the variable in their index vector is @xmath89 , which appears also as argument of the hpls . to obtain this unique form , we apply the following relations to the 2dhpls , which are all derived following the same lines as the formulae for the interchange of arguments discussed in the appendix of  @xcite :    1 .",

    "in this paper , we have presented analytic formulae for the two - loop virtual corrections to the process @xmath1 , which arise from the interference of the two - loop with the tree amplitude and from the self - interference of the one - loop amplitude . together with the contribution from the self - interference of the one - loop amplitudes for @xmath42  @xcite , these form the full @xmath12 corrections to the three - parton subprocess contribution to @xmath174  jets at nnlo .",
    "similar results can in principle be obtained for @xmath9-jet production in deep inelastic @xmath10 scattering or @xmath175-jet production in hadron ",
    "hadron collisions .",
    "however , the complexity of the cut structure of the non - planar graphs together with the rather different domains of convergence of the one- and two - dimensional harmonic polylogarithms makes this a non - trivial task , and we defer this to a later paper .",
    "it must also be kept in mind that these virtual corrections form only part of a full nnlo calculation , which also has to include the one - loop corrections to @xmath176  partons  @xcite where one of the partons becomes collinear or soft , as well as tree - level processes @xmath177  partons  @xcite with two soft or collinear partons . only after summing all these contributions ( and including terms from the renormalization of parton distributions for processes with partons in the initial state ) ,",
    "do the divergent terms cancel among one another .",
    "the factorization properties of both the one - loop , one - unresolved - parton contribution  @xcite and the tree - level , two - unresolved - parton contributions  @xcite have been studied , but a systematic procedure for isolating the infrared singularities has not been established .",
    "although this is still an open and highly non - trivial issue , significant progress is anticipated in the near future .",
    "the remaining finite terms must then be combined into a numerical program implementing the experimental definition of jet observables and event - shape variables . a first calculation involving the above features",
    "was presented for the case of photon - plus - one - jet final states in electron ",
    "positron annihilation in  @xcite , thus demonstrating the feasibility of this type of calculations .",
    "a prerequisite for such a numerical program is a stable and efficient next - to - leading order four - jet program , where the infrared singularities for the one - loop @xmath178  partons are combined with the tree - level @xmath13  parton with one parton unresolved .",
    "four such programs currently exist @xcite , each of which could be used as a starting point for a full @xmath0 nnlo three - jet program .",
    "tg and er would like to thank pierpaolo mastrolia for numerous discussions on the automatic derivation of symbolic reduction equations .",

    "ak thanks the university of durham for a research studentship .",
    "tg and ewng would like to acknowledge the hospitality of the workshop `` physics at tev colliders '' ( les houches , france , may 2001 ) , where this work was initiated .",

    "[ app : hpl ] the generalized polylogarithms @xmath190 of nielsen  @xcite turn out to be insufficient for the computation of multi - scale integrals beyond one loop . to overcome this limitation , one has to extend generalized polylogarithms to harmonic polylogarithms  @xcite .",
    "harmonic polylogarithms are obtained by the repeated integration of rational factors . if these rational factors contain , besides the integration variable , only constants , the resulting functions are one - dimensional harmonic polylogarithms ( or simply harmonic polylogarithms , hpls)@xcite . if the rational factors depend on a further variable , one obtains two - dimensional harmonic polylogarithms ( 2dhpls )  @xcite . in the following ,",
    "we define both classes of functions , and summarize their properties",
    ".      the hpls , introduced in @xcite , are one - variable functions @xmath191 depending , besides the argument @xmath192 , on a set of indices , grouped for convenience into the vector @xmath193 , whose components can take one of the three values @xmath194 and whose number is the weight @xmath195 of the hpl .",
    "more explicitly , the three hpls with @xmath196 are defined as @xmath197 their derivatives can be written as @xmath198 where the 3 rational fractions @xmath199 are given by @xmath200 for weight @xmath195 larger than 1 , write @xmath201 , where @xmath127 is the leftmost component of @xmath202 and @xmath203 stands for the vector of the remaining @xmath204 components .",
    "the harmonic polylogarithms of weight @xmath195 are then defined as follows : if all the @xmath195 components of @xmath205 take the value 0 , @xmath205 is said to take the value @xmath206 and @xmath207 while , if @xmath208 , @xmath209 in any case the derivatives can be written in the compact form @xmath210 where , again , @xmath127 is the leftmost component of @xmath211 and @xmath212 stands for the remaining @xmath204 components .",
    "it is immediate to see , from the very definition eq .",
    "( [ eq : defn0 ] ) , that there are @xmath213 hpls of weight @xmath195 , and that they are linearly independent .",
    "the hpls are generalizations of nielsen s polylogarithms  @xcite .",
    "the function @xmath214 , in nielsen s notation , is equal to the hpl whose first @xmath215 indices are all equal to 0 and the remaining @xmath216 indices all equal to 1 : @xmath217 in particular the euler polylogarithms @xmath218 correspond to @xmath219    as shown in @xcite , the product of two hpls of a same argument @xmath192 and weights @xmath220 can be expressed as a combination of hpls of that argument and weight @xmath221 , according to the product identity @xmath222 where @xmath223 stand for the @xmath216 and @xmath224 components of the indices of the two hpls , while @xmath225 represents all mergers of @xmath226 and @xmath227 into the vector @xmath228 with @xmath54 components , in which the relative orders of the elements of @xmath226 and @xmath227 are preserved .",
    "the explicit formulae relevant up to weight 4 are @xmath229 @xmath230 and @xmath231 where @xmath232 are indices taking any of the values @xmath194 .",
    "the formulae can be easily verified , one at a time , by observing that they are true at some specific point ( such as @xmath233 , where all the hpls vanish except in the otherwise trivial case in which all the indices are equal to 0 ) , then taking the @xmath192-derivatives of the two sides according to eq .",
    "( [ eq : derive ] ) and checking that they are equal ( using when needed the previously established lower - weight formulae ) .",
    "another class of identities is obtained by integrating ( [ eq : defh0 ] ) by parts . these integration - by - parts ( ibp ) identities",
    "read : @xmath234 these identities are not fully linearly independent from the product identities .",

    "are then defined as follows : if all the @xmath195 components of @xmath205 take the value 0 , @xmath205 is written as @xmath206 and @xmath247 while , if @xmath208 , @xmath248 in any case the derivatives can be written in the compact form @xmath249 where , again , @xmath127 is the leftmost component of @xmath211 and @xmath212 stands for the remaining @xmath204 components .",

    "<S> we compute the @xmath0 virtual qcd corrections to the @xmath1 matrix element arising from the interference of the two - loop with the tree - level amplitude and from the self - interference of the one - loop amplitude . </S>",
    "<S> the calculation is performed by reducing all loop integrals appearing in the two - loop amplitude to a small set of known master integrals . </S>",
    "<S> infrared and ultraviolet divergences are both regularized using conventional dimensional regularization , and the ultraviolet renormalization is performed in the @xmath2 scheme . </S>",
    "<S> the infrared pole structure of the matrix elements agrees with the prediction made by catani using an infrared factorization formula . </S>",
    "<S> the analytic result for the finite terms of both matrix elements is expressed in terms of one- and two - dimensional harmonic polylogarithms .    </S>",
    "<S> ippp/01/59 + dctp/01/118 + cern - th/2001 - 348 + hep - ph/0112081 + december 2001    3.5 cm    1.cm l.w .  </S>",
